<div id="review_32142527" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/32142527" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1406845-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1299600885p2/1406845.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/32142527?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/1406845-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer32142527" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8806629380489570282">At the end of the day, I liked Pandora's Star enough to finish it and continue with the second half of the story (Judas Unchained). However, this book took a loooong time to get going, and there were quite a few times when I was about ready to give up on it. There were also so many subplots that didn't seem to start connecting until near the end of the book, and were then finally realized in the sequel. I found it very easy to put down and forget about for a while, but I also found myself still </span>
  <span id="freeText8806629380489570282" style="display:none">At the end of the day, I liked Pandora's Star enough to finish it and continue with the second half of the story (Judas Unchained). However, this book took a loooong time to get going, and there were quite a few times when I was about ready to give up on it. There were also so many subplots that didn't seem to start connecting until near the end of the book, and were then finally realized in the sequel. I found it very easy to put down and forget about for a while, but I also found myself still picking it back up to read it.<br /><br />On the positive side, Hamilton certainly has a rich imagination! A lot of the technology he envisioned was very interesting, and the alien species - particularly the antagonist - were very different and quite interesting. For some folks who are interested in visions of future technology, it might be worth a read just for that alone.<br /><br />The bottom line for me is that this is worth a read, but be prepared for a very long book that ends - literally - halfway through the story when things are finally starting to get good. So just plan ahead to pick up Judas Unchained to find out what happens.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8806629380489570282" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/11960925?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781405000208" href="/book/show/866135.Pandora_s_Star">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">SciFi fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/748293-radu-stanculescu?shelf=sf">sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/748293-radu-stanculescu?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer11960925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17145855414231178305">Don't be fooled by the separation of the "Commonwealth Saga" into two books (this one and "Judas Unchained"). It's just a big-big book, so know that if you're starting this one you'll have a total of about 2000 pages to read. :)<br/><br/>More "mature" and with a more refined style than the "Night's Dawn" trilogy, the "Commonwealth Saga" is still a mix of a good number of different story lines that flow towards a (very distant) convergence point. It's got some pretty "alien" aliens, good humour and interes</span>
  <span id="freeText17145855414231178305" style="display:none">Don't be fooled by the separation of the "Commonwealth Saga" into two books (this one and "Judas Unchained"). It's just a big-big book, so know that if you're starting this one you'll have a total of about 2000 pages to read. :)<br /><br />More "mature" and with a more refined style than the "Night's Dawn" trilogy, the "Commonwealth Saga" is still a mix of a good number of different story lines that flow towards a (very distant) convergence point. It's got some pretty "alien" aliens, good humour and interesting ideas to keep you company throughout the story. I've yet to read "Misspent Youth" (set in the same universe, only much earlier) and "The Dreaming Void" (first book of the "Void" trilogy, later in the same universe), but I'll definitely give them a try.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1572133291" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1572133291" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1572133291?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447279662" href="/book/show/24913200-pandora-s-star">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19126246-kaitlin?shelf=sci-fi-2016">sci-fi-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1572133291" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2389432832313019097">This book was my first forray into the work of Hamilton, a very well-established Science Fiction writer. Sadly, although I think some of Hamilton's ideas are super interesting and would make for a hugely complex and exciting Universe, these good ideas are so few and far between in amongst the 1,000+ page length that with the time it took to get to the next 'moment' I had already lost my excitement for the last one. I am definitely not afraid of a big book, in fact big books are some of my favour</span>
  <span id="freeText2389432832313019097" style="display:none">This book was my first forray into the work of Hamilton, a very well-established Science Fiction writer. Sadly, although I think some of Hamilton's ideas are super interesting and would make for a hugely complex and exciting Universe, these good ideas are so few and far between in amongst the 1,000+ page length that with the time it took to get to the next 'moment' I had already lost my excitement for the last one. I am definitely not afraid of a big book, in fact big books are some of my favourite ones and so I had truly hoped to love this. Sadly, I just think that this style of Sci-Fi isn't my personal taste and reading an epic tome with a huge cast, a lot of complex technology, and a setting that spans Galaxies, I just couldn't wrap my head around it all. I know a lot of people say that the Malazan series by Erikson is hard to get to grips with, for me, this was a hell of a lot harder to get excited by and even when I was excited, that tension was soon lost by the sheer page length.<br /><br />This story has a huge amount of characters and I couldn't begin to list them all here but I will discuss some of the more important ones and those who I followed with interest. The first two characters, Ozzie and Orion, are my favourite from the entire book. These two become part of a big adventure following the 'paths' (an alien pathway between worlds and no-one really knows where they lead to). I genuinely found the mentor/mentee relationship here to be interesting and I liked the dynamic that the two of them found as the story went on and they found their rhythm. I also felt as though there was actually stuff happening in their story every time I was a part of it, and throughout the whole book their story was the only one which I consistently tuned into and found cool.<br />The next character I liked was MorningLightMountain and I will admit this is largely due to the name. MorningLightMountain is a being of enormous power and intellect who exists in the far regions of deep space, away from where the Commonwealth (a selection of planets inhabited by Humans and Aliens in harmony) is situated. This being and the way they interpreted the actions of humans fascinated me, and I do think there were some genuinely vibrant moments in this plot, however, it just didn't make up for the over-complication of some of the scenes.<br />We also have Kime who is a Captain from many generations past. Kime is enlisted on a mission to go to a far off barrier which has been discovered in Space and see if he and his team are able to find out what is behind this barrier. Little does he or the team know that there may be far more than they bargained on hidden away, and it may be hidden for a reason (this is the major thread of the story which most of the characters connect to).<br />We also have Paula, a detective on the hunt for a long-time offender who is repeatedly escaping her clutches and foiling her attempts to capture him. Her story had a few ups, but was mostly dead boring for me sadly.<br />Melanie and Justine are two of the other female characters we meet and I have to say I found both to be non-genuine and irritating at different times (particularly Melanie who was just a complete annoyance to me). <br />We have various other people who have important status too and some of the aliens we meet caused me great amusement becuase of how they functioned, but I just couldn't tell you everyone or we would be here forever.<br /><br />There were a few good things and one of these which I did like was the modification ideas and rejuvenation. Within this Commonwealth people have the ability to live forever and become re-born every few decades if they have the money to pay for it. They upload their memories so that their newly made bodies can keep the memories, and they start living their life again maybe in a new job, area or with new friends, lovers etc. This idea was cool to me and made for some really old cool characters who had a wealth of knowledge.<br />We also have things like the Alien races who definitely interested me a lot.<br /><br />Sadly the good was far outweighed by overly-complex Space tech mumbo-jumbo which I didn't either care about or didn't understand. I appreciate you don't have to 'get' everything in a SF book as it's supposed to be fictional, but I like when I can comprehend how things work and why they work that way and what their use is, and I felt that often things weren't explained to a level where this worked for me.<br />I also felt that this book was way too huge for what actually happened. Maybe this is supposed to focus on the technology and characters more than the plot, I don't know, but for me it took a long time to even set up a plot and settle into it, and when it did it was so fragmented with all the povs that I still couldn't connect to it.<br /><br />I read this with a few other friends and a few of them read 100ish pages and then dropped out. I finished this, and yet I do wish I had dropped out at pg 100ish as for me it just did not come together in a satisfying way and everything that did happen wasn't enough to make up for the amount of dead-weight pages which bored me. Sadly, I won't be investing in or reading any more Peter F Hamilton in the future unless it's novella length as this one was just way too intense for not enough return. 2*s overall and that's only for the few cool elements which I did like. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2389432832313019097" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3001988057" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3001988057" />
    <a title="Cathy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/978552-cathy"><img alt="Cathy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604572841p2/978552.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3001988057?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cathy" href="/user/show/978552-cathy">Cathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345479211" href="/book/show/526307.Pandora_s_Star">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/978552-cathy?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3001988057" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer355387364944895185">This is a very long book and really should be read with the plan to continue with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45244.Judas_Unchained' title='Judas Unchained by Peter F. Hamilton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Judas Unchained</a>. The story unfolds with the speed of a geriatric snail, so bring patience and time and appreciation for the little things along. I took me two months to get through the audiobook—ok, I am slow with audio—and I did it with the print version next to me, to double-check on details. <br/>The world building is great, this is full of great ideas. And when there is action, it is well done. Characters take their</span>
  <span id="freeText355387364944895185" style="display:none">This is a very long book and really should be read with the plan to continue with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45244.Judas_Unchained" title="Judas Unchained by Peter F. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Judas Unchained</a>. The story unfolds with the speed of a geriatric snail, so bring patience and time and appreciation for the little things along. I took me two months to get through the audiobook—ok, I am slow with audio—and I did it with the print version next to me, to double-check on details. <br />The world building is great, this is full of great ideas. And when there is action, it is well done. Characters take their time to develop and the aliens are truly scary in their otherness. This is good, although I wonder what it would be like at half the page count...<br /><br />Thoughts and comments, while working my way through this monster:<br />————<br />Audiobook Part 1: 6 h 56 min (183 pages), Chapters 1-6, ★★★½☆<br />Glacially slow set-up and introduction of a variety of characters. Very little plot progression. I liked what was there. Alas, it was not for the impatient and easily bored (aka ME!). I wonder how all these very different stories will come together.<br /><br />Chapter list with characters behind the tag: <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />- Prologue<br />NASA Captain-Pilot Wilson Kime, stepping on Mars in third place...<br />Nigel Sheldon and college geek with wild Afro (Ozzie), appearing in an opening in space...<br /><br />- Chapter One<br />Dudley Bose and the vanishing star...<br />Dyson Alpha, the vanishing star...<br />Lion Walker Eyre, man with a telescope.<br /><br />- Chapter Two<br />Adam Elvin, man of mystery and many faces, weapons procurer.<br />Nigel Murphy, a comrade with weapons. <br />Sabbah, undercover comrade.<br />Rachael Lancier, arms dealer.<br />Chief Investigator Paula Myo.<br />Don Mares and Maggie Lidsey, Police detectives. <br />Tarlo and Renne, Investigators from the Directorate.<br /><br />- Chapter Three<br />Rafael Columbia, chief of the Intersolar Serious Crimes Directorate. Bunch of other committee members.<br />Tara Jennifer Shaheef, woman out of luck.<br />Wyobie Cotal, lover boy.<br /><br />- Chapter Four<br />Justine Burnelli, having fun with a hyperglider. Her friend Estella.<br />Kazimir McFoster, wild man in a kilt.<br /><br />- Chapter Five<br />Wilson Kime again, retired. Emily, his grand daughter.<br />Paula Myo, chasing Elvin...<br />Wyobie Cotal again, diminished...<br /><br />- Chapter Six<br />Mark Vernon, fist lifer on Augusta.<br />Liz, his beautiful wife, not a first lifer...<br />Barry, their son. Sandy, baby girl.<br />Marty, Mark‘s dad, and Amanda, his girlfriend. Slightly scandalous.<br />Tarlo and Renne again, investigating...<br />April Gallar Halgarth, girl with memory problems. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />————<br />Audiobook Part 2: 7 h 22 min (pages 184-376), Chapter 7-11, ★★★★★<br />Interesting biology and chemistry! Really cool idea, although Merredin is not necessarily a planet I would like to visit. Just that by itself is a great plot bunny for a colonization/first contact novel! There are several other planets and constructs in this part of the book, that would make for great settings for separate novels. The world building here is fascinating. <br /><br />With all people living multiple lives, I would love to have a timeline sketched out at the back of the book. If I should ever decide to re-read this book, I plan to make annotations and try to figure out a timeline myself.<br /><br />You definitely need patience with this book. Interesting things happen and then you switch POV and.... something else happens and it‘s all a very loooong game....<br /> <br />But by Chapter 10 (yes, yes, almost 300 pages of set-up), things are starting to come together, the many characters are becoming familiar names and the plot picks up the pace.<br /><br />Chapter list with characters, settings and spoilery ramblings: <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />- Chapter Seven<br />Oscar Monroe, wormhole builder and planetary explorer, showing up again on Merredin.<br />Dudley Bose, Leonida City, discoverer of astronomical phenomena, feeling entitled... His wife Wendy and Brad, with Earle, the News man, no last name... <br /><br />- Chapter Eight<br />Ozzie Fernandez Isaac, on his asteroid and travelling the Path.<br />Nine Sky, the elf...ehem... Silfen.<br />Orion, the orphan boy.<br /><br />Elves! Who could say no to that! Silvergalde is a more tempting planet. And down the rabbit hole we go! <br /><br />- Chapter Nine<br />Adam Elvin showing up again, on Lothian. Very Scottish...<br />Bradley Johansson—I feel like I should know him from a previous chapter.<br />Tara Jennifer Shaheef and her new husband, deSavoel.<br />Morton, Tara‘s Ex. His girlfriend Melanie.<br /><br />Starting to wonder. Well, continuing to wonder... why Tara and Wyobie were killed. And I am also starting to want a timeline... Morton has been rejuvenated twice since Tara‘s death and mentioned 40 years since....<br /><br />- Chapter 10<br />Oscar Monroe (wormhole builder, chapter 7), McClain Gilbert, and the High Angel—another very cool idea worthy of its own novel.<br />Paula and Hoshe, meeting the Raiel and passing Tara‘s memories to Qatux. Another cool concept. Human ethics. Judging others through your own lens—should you or shouldn‘t you?<br />Ron Tannie, regretting taking this job on Anshun. Wowza, this is the action I like to see in a good SF opera! And well played, Wilson!<br />Lennie Al Husan, reporter on Anshun—at this point I wonder if all these seemingly random characters will end up as personnel and passengers on the Second Chance?<br /><br />- Chapter 11<br />Meeting Sara and old Bill, the Korrok-hi. Cocktail hour on the ice planet.<br />Rafael Columbia shows up again and proves to be an idiot that Paula is not too fussed with.<br />At this point in the narrative, I would say that Ozzie is one of my favourite characters. Together with Wilson and Paula Myo. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />————<br />Audiobook Part 3: 7 h 30 min (pages 377-574), Chapters 12-16, ★★★★☆<br />The characters are finally familiar and we are getting into the meat of the story.<br /><br />————<br />Audiobook Part 4: 8 h 52 min (pages 575-806), Chapters 17-21, ★★★★☆<br />Chapter 18 was horrific! We are moving towards a climax... maybe... Besides the action I still enjoyed Ozzie‘s chapters the most.<br /><br />————<br />Audiobook Part 5: 6 h 48 min (pages 807-988), Chapters 22-25, ★★★★☆<br />Wow, I finished! I thought this would never end. There was some light wrapping up of the status quo at the end, but I guess it would be a good strategy to have Judas Unchained ready to go! I pretty much continued with the audio straight away.<br /><br />————<br />On the Marie Celeste of the Commonwealth universe: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://peterfhamilton.fandom.com/wiki/Marie_Celeste">https://peterfhamilton.fandom.com/wik...</a><br />And the RL Mary Celeste: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mary_Celeste">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mary_Ce...</a><br /><br />The Commonwealth, publication order:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/108563-commonwealth-universe">https://www.goodreads.com/series/1085...</a></span>

<div id="review_165308118" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/165308118" />
    <a title="Daniel Roy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5368477-daniel-roy"><img alt="Daniel Roy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513163643p2/5368477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/165308118?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel Roy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel Roy" href="/user/show/5368477-daniel-roy">Daniel Roy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345479211" href="/book/show/526307.Pandora_s_Star">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5368477-daniel-roy?shelf=sf">sf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer165308118" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5203421258751789938">Being a huge fan of the 'Night's Dawn' trilogy, I was naturally very happy to get my hands on this book. If you liked 'Night's Dawn', there's a chance you will find something to your liking in here - but don't expect anything approaching the quality of 'The Neutronium Alchemist'.<br/><br/>In this series (completed by 'Judas Unchained' next year), Hamilton seems to set out to do something similar to what he did in 'Night's Dawn': present a riveting, complex world and then take a sledgehammer to it. The uni</span>
  <span id="freeText5203421258751789938" style="display:none">Being a huge fan of the 'Night's Dawn' trilogy, I was naturally very happy to get my hands on this book. If you liked 'Night's Dawn', there's a chance you will find something to your liking in here - but don't expect anything approaching the quality of 'The Neutronium Alchemist'.<br /><br />In this series (completed by 'Judas Unchained' next year), Hamilton seems to set out to do something similar to what he did in 'Night's Dawn': present a riveting, complex world and then take a sledgehammer to it. The universe in 'Pandora's Star' sure is awfully detailed, and parts of it (such as the trains that travel between worlds) are surely fascinating.<br /><br />However, the world just doesn't click as neatly as 'Night's Dawn', and I was left with the feeling that, as detailed as this novel was, I just didn't buy into it. There's a LOT of pages in this book used to describe the world, but instead of being mesmerising, they tend to be very frustrating as the author takes the reader by the hand to guide him through yet another human colony vaguely based on Western places, such as Venice or California.<br /><br />I think this is one of these books that would have benefited from having less, not more. Some parts were very carefully crafted and interesting, while other sub-plots were frustrating for being so boring and leading nowhere. In some cases (the fanfic-level chapter on the court case of a rich businessman, to quote one) was so poorly written and so unappealing that they almost convinced me to put down the book and pick up something else.<br /><br />Because of the number of secondary characters in the novel, some characters become such clichés that they`re actually painful to read. Mark, the "everyday normal guy" witnessing the events of the novel in the midst of his very boring life, made me groan every time his name showed up. Mellanie, the nubian naive girl who gets mistreated by the rich man she loves blindly, was also very painful to read so stereotypical she was. It's a pity, because they ultimately bury great characters such as Nigel Sheldon or Ozzie, that show a bit more fleshing out. Oh, and to show you how poorly fleshed-out these secondary characters turned out to be, I was unable to find one woman in the novel that was not somehow beautiful and closer to a man's fantasy than an actual believeable woman.<br /><br />Still; throughout all these gripes is an interesting bit of space opera waiting to unfold. The beauty of 'Night's Dawn' was to see a fully realized world fall to pieces under a new threat. 'Judas Unchained' promises to do exactly that to the world of 'Pandora's Star'. This promise has kept me going through this very long novel: that all I read so far was preparation for Peter Hamilton taking an awesome sledgehammer to his carefully constructed world. That is not to say I harbor fantasies of revenge upon this long novel, but rather that this long preparation might be worth it once Hamilton turns things upside down.<br /><br />If the followup is up to par with Hamilton's previous works, then this novel might be worth slowly wading through. Here's hoping that it will be: because Pandora's Star in itself is ambitious, but so flawed that it failed to fire up my imagination and really engage me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5203421258751789938" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1125188064" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1125188064" />
    <a title="spikeINflorida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24788985-spikeinflorida"><img alt="spikeINflorida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585338304p2/24788985.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1125188064?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="spikeINflorida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="spikeINflorida" href="/user/show/24788985-spikeinflorida">spikeINflorida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1125188064" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer25335392702823150">Five stars for the perilous wormhole jouneys of Captain Kime and his good ship and crew. And for the Prime aliens and their war mongering leader Morning-LightMountain. THIS is why I read SF. Unfortunately this engrossing part of the story played second fiddle to a whole lotta soapy space opera. <br/>Four stars for Ozzie's dream-like trek across multiple worlds via the Silfen paths, man.<br/>Three stars for ultra-uber Detective Myo and her perpetual investigation of radical kilt-wearin' terrorists and the </span>
  <span id="freeText25335392702823150" style="display:none">Five stars for the perilous wormhole jouneys of Captain Kime and his good ship and crew. And for the Prime aliens and their war mongering leader Morning-LightMountain. THIS is why I read SF. Unfortunately this engrossing part of the story played second fiddle to a whole lotta soapy space opera. <br />Four stars for Ozzie's dream-like trek across multiple worlds via the Silfen paths, man.<br />Three stars for ultra-uber Detective Myo and her perpetual investigation of radical kilt-wearin' terrorists and the mystical Starflyer. <br />Two stars for gold digging Mellanie and her god-like partner. And eco-friendly Mark and his oh-so-cute family...and puppy!<br />One star for a morbidly obese book that is in dire need of a major liposuction edit. A thousand pages? C'mon, man!</span>
  <a data-text-id="25335392702823150" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1894671734" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1894671734" />
    <a title="Anirudh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16686132-anirudh"><img alt="Anirudh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1359010972p2/16686132.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1894671734?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anirudh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anirudh" href="/user/show/16686132-anirudh">Anirudh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16686132-anirudh?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1894671734" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12803704009740342167">Pandora's Star, being my first serious venture into science fiction was a lucky pick and did not disappoint. This is truly an epic space opera having a vast amount of characters, grand design, drama, action and of course science beyond imagination. I do not know if what the author explains is scientifically possible, but it is definitely thoroughly entertaining. <br/><br/><b>1. Plot</b> Without giving away too many spoilers, the story revolves around man's discovery of worm holes, a method to travel vast distanc</span>
  <span id="freeText12803704009740342167" style="display:none">Pandora's Star, being my first serious venture into science fiction was a lucky pick and did not disappoint. This is truly an epic space opera having a vast amount of characters, grand design, drama, action and of course science beyond imagination. I do not know if what the author explains is scientifically possible, but it is definitely thoroughly entertaining. <br /><br /><b>1. Plot</b> Without giving away too many spoilers, the story revolves around man's discovery of worm holes, a method to travel vast distances with ease and the subsequent exploration and colonisation of man. The story begins when man discovers 2 stars which have been sealed off by an unknown entity and his curiosity to know what lies beyond. Hamilton has a very interesting story to tell, a story that has multiple elements going well for it. (though not all) The sheer size of this story is daunting but equally enthralling. From the mysterious encounters with the aliens to the fighting clans of Far away the story has a wide variety of sub stories to offer. However some of the stories drag on and hinder the pace of the main story. It would seems all stories will connect at some point in the next book, for now we wait.<br /><br /><b>2. World Building</b> This is undoubtedly the strongest aspect of the book. Hamilton truly brings out a world where humans have spread out like a virus infecting every planet they come across, exploiting it and despite the abundance of resources bickering and fighting albeit in a more modern way. I don’t know if it was intended but as I read it I felt it was an interesting reflection on man and no matter how developed he gets he does not let go of his primitive instincts. <br /><br />Another concept that was really interesting was the fate of death. Science has changed the way man looks at death entirely, reducing it to somewhat of a temporary inconvenience. This, while being a fascinating concept had the risk of ruining the tension or fear from the story as any harm can be repaired. However Hamilton manages it well and at the end does indeed bring out the fear in men despite all their technological advancement and makes it believable.<br /><br />There is another interesting concept of SI the self aware artificial intelligence and it’s interaction with humans. There are of course much more Hamilton has to offer but one must read the book to discover them<br /><br /><b>3. Characters</b> Pandora’s star being driven mainly by the story does little to explore characters beyond what is required to continue the story. However one cannot find fault in this approach as character exploration would not have suited this style of storytelling. <br /><br /><b>4. Narration</b> Hamilton is not the best of narrators. His style is quite straight forward and lacks the charms of word play or wit. This is a book where story takes precedence over all else. He does manage to build up tension with the main story but that’s about it. The switch between the main plot and side stories do not transition smoothly, this is especially true for the detective’s story which throws off the momentum of the space exploration quite a bit. I did not mind the length of the book however, that was something the reader is aware of before he begins reading. <br /><br /><b>5. Aliens</b> I believe this requires a special mention. The main antagonist in the story is very unique and extremely well crafted. The first encounter with them is undoubtedly my favourite portion of the book. It is a sheer pleasure to read how two entirely different species react to the existence of the other. <br /><br />This is definitely a book worth exploring. Get your laser guns, jump on your spaceships and be ready to sail to infinity and beyond. <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12803704009740342167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1943505125526367879">Well then. I hope that book reviews don't need to be a length that's proportional to the size of the book being reviewed. Actually, I can safely say that this one definitely won't be.<br/><br/>Damn, that was a big tome. And as much as I like John Lee, I need a new reader in my next book. Between this and <i>Revelation Space</i>, I've heard John Lee's voice more this year than any member of my family's voice. My wife does say I can tune her out, and unfortunately I think this happened with Mr. Lee as well for lar</span>
  <span id="freeText1943505125526367879" style="display:none">Well then. I hope that book reviews don't need to be a length that's proportional to the size of the book being reviewed. Actually, I can safely say that this one definitely won't be.<br /><br />Damn, that was a big tome. And as much as I like John Lee, I need a new reader in my next book. Between this and <i>Revelation Space</i>, I've heard John Lee's voice more this year than any member of my family's voice. My wife does say I can tune her out, and unfortunately I think this happened with Mr. Lee as well for large parts of the book.<br /><br />There were great parts, and great characters. Then there were long periods of slog and yawn. What's bad is that my brain had zoned out and gone elsewhere during some of the longer slogs, and ended up missing some of the good parts. I can't say how many times I'd regain focus and be like "when did they switch to that character?"<br /><br />I feel like I need some CliffNotes. There were things I wanted to know more about, but missed the connections. I mean, sometimes I'd be listening and be thinking, "just who is this character?" even though I knew I'd read about them earlier. It just had been so long....<br /><br />And this is only half the story. Ouch. I definitely need some CliffNotes before I tackle <i>Judas Unchained</i>. Probably some NoDoze too.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9615049848935557893">I quite enjoyed Pandora's Star, and the vast universe Peter F. Hamilton creates. Where many science fiction writers take one significant technological advance and write about how their world would change around that, Hamilton has explored numerous game-changing advances all at once, and tried to see what wormhole travel/body rejuvenation/memory download would together do to a rapidly expanding human Commonwealth of planets.<br/><br/>Note: The rest of this review has been withdrawn due to the changes in Go</span>
  <span id="freeText9615049848935557893" style="display:none">I quite enjoyed Pandora's Star, and the vast universe Peter F. Hamilton creates. Where many science fiction writers take one significant technological advance and write about how their world would change around that, Hamilton has explored numerous game-changing advances all at once, and tried to see what wormhole travel/body rejuvenation/memory download would together do to a rapidly expanding human Commonwealth of planets.<br /><br />Note: The rest of this review has been withdrawn due to the changes in Goodreads policy and enforcement.     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_793379325" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793379325" />
    <a title="Dara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13656026-dara"><img alt="Dara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500476380p2/13656026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/793379325?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dara" href="/user/show/13656026-dara">Dara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6136470-pandora-s-star">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13656026-dara?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13656026-dara?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13656026-dara?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13656026-dara?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13656026-dara?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13656026-dara?shelf=lady-protag">lady-protag</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer793379325" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11538131947647426187">At 1,144 pages, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45252.Pandora_s_Star' title='Pandora's Star by Peter F. Hamilton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pandora's Star</a> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25375.Peter_F__Hamilton' title='Peter F. Hamilton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Peter F. Hamilton</a> is not a casual read. Hamilton uses all of those pages to create a rich and detailed future of the human race. Entertaining, frustrating, and exhilarating, Pandora's Star slowly pulls the reader into it's grasp and doesn't let go.<br/><br/><i>Pandora's Star</i> has a lot of characters and plenty of points-of-view, making it a little daunting at first. That said, Hamilton does a great job of making each character distinct and interesting. Even characters I initi</span>
  <span id="freeText11538131947647426187" style="display:none">At 1,144 pages, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45252.Pandora_s_Star" title="Pandora's Star by Peter F. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Pandora's Star</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25375.Peter_F__Hamilton" title="Peter F. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Peter F. Hamilton</a> is not a casual read. Hamilton uses all of those pages to create a rich and detailed future of the human race. Entertaining, frustrating, and exhilarating, Pandora's Star slowly pulls the reader into it's grasp and doesn't let go.<br /><br /><i>Pandora's Star</i> has a lot of characters and plenty of points-of-view, making it a little daunting at first. That said, Hamilton does a great job of making each character distinct and interesting. Even characters I initially didn't like, I ended up excited to read about them and caring about their fates by the end of the novel.<br /><br />The plot starts with a pair of stars disappearing behind a massive barrier. Naturally, humans must go poke at it. The main plot involving the disappearance didn't click for me until about half-way through. There are other plot threads which start to connect and interweave in ways that aren't entirely clear yet but this is the first book in a rather large duology.<br /><br />There's a lot of world-building done in the best way: showing and not telling. Hamilton shows the readers through his character's eyes how the Commonwealth operates. We learn about their technology, history, culture, and different ways of life through experiences with the characters.<br /><br />In the Commonwealth, humans don't really die anymore. There's a process called rejuvenation where people go for a new, young version of their body when they reach a certain age and then are young again. I would have liked to know a bit more about the process but Hamilton doesn't delve into the science of how it works.<br /><br />The plot really picks up around the half-way mark. The first half is a lot of setup and character introduction. We meet the main players of the Dynasty families who have enormous amounts of wealth and power such as Nigel Sheldon, Ozzie Issacs, and the Burnelli family, investigator Paula Myo, Admiral Wilson Kime, and reporter Mellanie Rescorai. This builds a great foundation for the story but at times really drags on and becomes tedious.<br /><br />The characters are mostly all human but aliens are present in Hamilton's universe. There is a race called the Silfen which are almost like space elves. They're rather mystical but also quite frightening. The alien species play a larger part in the sequel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45244.Judas_Unchained" title="Judas Unchained by Peter F. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Judas Unchained</a>.<br /><br />The book ends on a riveting cliffhanger which I will not spoil here. Needless to say, it prompted me to immediately pick up the second novel.<br /><br /><i>Pandora's Star</i> is a slow burn of a book with fascinating characters, interesting storylines, and a deep and substantial world. Any sci-fi fan would be doing themselves a service by picking this up.<br /><br /><b>B</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11538131947647426187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8720101081686795849">Oh boy, this was really not an easy book to get through. About 1/3 was really interesting, 1/3 was OK, and the other 1/3 was "this book is long enough without adding stuff that doesn't seem to matter much." The thing that finally killed it for me though, was the last page. I thought I would finally see some resolution for my favourite story thread and...no. I have to read the OTHER HALF of the story to get that, namely, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45244.Judas_Unchained' title='Judas Unchained by Peter F. Hamilton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Judas Unchained</a>.<br/><br/>I don't know that I have the stamina for Round 2.</span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_89187'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/89187.Revelation_Space"><img alt="Revelation Space (Revelation Space, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1405532042l/89187._SY160_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NE8V724YSdjS7bWnrcUZed1JhiJga466mR2dwUh2X61wBgJtvysLj3eW9XgPtYdEI+ESBtIBnJuSdm67/26cDg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fLLV4d7UjfBGNSjJwboZcDeA5ObMdK4TjwhrIilBluE4+8JjD+fPp+NOaBZjyodNyShwwn4evDKEY5hYnllVQg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer9235641339890579677">Peter F. Hamilton is a British science fiction author. He is best known for writing space opera. As of the publication of his tenth novel in 2004, his works had sold over two million copies worldwide, making him Britain's biggest-selling science fiction author.</span>

Coexistence is impossible with the technologically advanced aliens, who are genetically hardwired to exterminate all other forms of life. Twenty-three planets have already fallen to the invaders, with casualties in the hundreds of millions. And no one knows when or where the genocidal Prime will strike next. \n\nNor are the Prime the only threat. For more than a hundred years, a shadowy cult, the Guardians of Selfhood, has warned that an alien with mind-control abilities impossible to detect or resist -- the Starflyer -- has secretly infiltrated the Commonwealth. Branded as terrorists, the Guardians and their leader, Bradley Johansson, have been hunted by relentless investigator Paula Myo. But now evidence suggests that the Guardians were right all along, and that the Starflyer has placed agents in vital posts throughout the Commonwealth -- agents who are now sabotaging the war effort. \n\nIs the Starflyer an ally of the Prime, or has it orchestrated a fight to the death between the two species for its own advantage?
